Objections and Extensions: The Proof Applied to Descending Series
Extends the proof to descending series and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second proof applies to descending series of effects and how an objection regarding the cause of the aggregate is refuted.

Core Idea
The proof works for descending series too; the aggregate of effects must have a cause outside the series.

The author now addresses a potential objection: in a descending chain, each member is both cause and effect, so the aggregate might cause itself. He shows this is impossible and reaffirms the proof's validity for both directions.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the passage that begins with the objection about descending effects.
Notice the subtlety: each individual is a cause in one respect and an effect in another.
2
Analyze the argument
The objection suggests the cause of the aggregate could be internal, but the author argues this leads to self-causation or a cut in the series.
3
Understand the refutation
The author shows that the proof indeed applies to descending series, despite the objection, and clarifies the necessity of an external cause.
The final remark distinguishes between necessity and suitability in assuming the second series.

First Argument Against Infinite Regress: Self-Causation
Sanusi presents the first argument against infinite regress via self-causation reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first rational proof that infinite regress is impossible, specifically how it reduces to the absurdity of self-causation.

Core Idea
An infinite regress of causes forces a cause to be its own cause—impossible.

This lesson introduces the classic kalam argument against an infinite chain of contingent causes. Before we can affirm a Creator, we must show that an endless regress of causes is logically impossible. The first argument uses a reductio: assuming a complete chain leads to a cause causing itself, which is absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage Carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: a thesis, a hypothetical, a conclusion, and a final note.
The author uses very precise logical language.
2
Identify the Reductio Structure
Identify the assumption made (that the cause before the last effect is independent creator of the whole chain) and the absurd conclusion drawn (it would be cause of itself). Understand why this is impossible.
Self-causation is logically impossible.
3
Note the Scope Restriction
The author explicitly states that this proof only works for ascending chains of causes, not descending chains of effects. Understand why this distinction matters.
This prevents a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة قبله بمرتبة واحدة وهكذا ؛ لأنه لو كان ما قبل المعلول الأخير علة موجدة للسلسلة بأسرها مستقلة بالتأثير فيها حقيقة لكان علة لنفسه قطعاً. واعلم أن هذا الدليل إنما يجري في تسلسل الممكنات متصاعدة في العلل لا متنازلة في المعلولات كما لا يخفى على ذي فكرة .
The Fifth Observatory - The Eighth Objective: Infinite regress is impossible: that the contingent should depend on a cause [that is] before it by one rank, and so on; because if what is before the last effect were a cause bringing the entire chain into existence, independent in its influence over it in reality, it would inevitably be a cause of itself. And know that this proof only applies to an ascending regress of contingents in causes, not to a descending one in effects, as is not hidden from one who reflects.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument (al-wajh al-awwal) against infinite regress (tasalsul). It begins by stating the impossibility of an infinite chain where each contingent depends on a cause preceding it by one rank, and so on ad infinitum. The proof is a reductio: if the cause immediately preceding the last effect were the sole and independent creator of the entire chain in reality, then it would be the cause of itself—which is absurd. The argument then notes a limitation: this proof only works for ascending chains (where causes go upwards to a first cause), not for descending chains (where effects go downwards from a cause). The author warns that this is obvious to anyone who thinks. The passage is a concise statement of the classic kalam argument that an infinite regress of causes would entail self-causation, which is impossible.

Key Terms
التسلسل
العلة
المعلول
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument also applies to descending chains of effects.
Correction: The author explicitly states that this proof only works for ascending chains of causes, not descending ones.

Checkpoint
Why does the first argument against infinite regress lead to a contradiction?
A) It implies a circle of causes.
B) It entails that something would be the cause of itself.
C) It requires an infinite number of causes.
D) It assumes a first cause exists.

Key Takeaway
The first argument against infinite regress shows that an independent cause of the entire chain would self-cause, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the chain of causes in your own existence—your parents, their parents, teachers, events, circumstances. Do you ever feel that you are self-made or that you are the cause of your own success? How does Sanusi's argument about self-causation challenge that feeling? What does it force you to acknowledge about the true source of everything you are and have?
?
If you truly believe that nothing can be its own cause, then what must be the ultimate cause of your own contingent existence? How would it change the way you live today if you really internalized that you are not self-sufficient but entirely dependent on a First Cause?
?
This argument is purely logical, not emotional. But consider: the very ability to reason through this proof is a gift you did not give yourself. When you finish studying this lesson, will you take a moment to thank the One who gave you the mind to understand it? Or will you simply move on to the next task, treating this truth as mere information?

Burhan al-Tatbiq: Correlating Infinite Series to Refute Regress
Introduces Burhan al-Tatbiq and explains its method for two cases of correlation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the method of Burhan al-Tatbiq and how it refutes infinite regress in both causes and effects.

Core Idea
Correlating two infinite series forces them to be finite—that is the proof.

The concept of infinite regress poses a challenge to arguments for God's existence. Theologians developed several proofs against it. The second proof, Burhan al-Tatbiq (Proof of Correlation), is considered the strongest because it applies to many types of series, whether ordered or not. In this passage, the author explains how the proof works by correlating two supposedly infinite series and showing that a contradiction arises.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation, to get the flow of the argument.
Notice the two cases that follow the correlation.
2
Understand the setup
Two infinite series are assumed: one exceeding the other by a finite number. This setup is crucial for the proof.
The series can be ascending (causes) or descending (effects).
3
Follow the correlation method
Correlate the two series from a common starting point: match first with first, second with second, and so on.
4
Examine the two cases
Case 1: One-to-one correspondence leads to equality, contradicting excess. Case 2: An unmatched part causes the deficient series to cut off, making it finite.
Either way, the assumption of infinitude fails.
5
Note the scope of the proof
The proof applies to successive and simultaneous, ordered and unordered series. That makes it comprehensive.
This addresses a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه (الثاني) من وجوه إبطال التسلسل (أنا نفرض من معلول (ما ) بطريق التصاعد ) إلى غير النهاية جملة ومما قبله بمتناه إلى غير النهاية جملة أخرى، هذا إذا كان التسلسل في جانب العلل، وإذا كان في جانب المعلولات فرضنا من علة معينة بطريق التنازل إلى غير النهاية جملة ومما بعدها بمتناه إلى غير النهاية جملة أخرى فيحصل هناك جملتان غير متناهيتين إحداهما زائدة على الأخرى بعدد متناه. (ثم نطبق الجملتين ) أي إحداهما على الأخرى ( من ذلك المبدأ أي من ذلك الجانب الذي لكل واحدة منهما فيه مبدأ، فالأول) من إحداهما ( بالأول ) أي بإزاء الأول من الأخرى ) والثاني بالثاني، وهلم جراً. فإن كان بإزاء كل واحد من الجملة ( الزائدة واحد من الجملة ( الناقصة ) في عدة الآحاد كانت الناقصة كالزائدة ) ، أي مساوية لها في عدة الآحاد، ( وهذا خلف . وإلا ) أي وإن لم يكن بإزاء كل واحد من الزائدة واحد من الناقصة، ( وجد في الزائدة جزء لا يوجد بإزائه في الناقصة شيء، وعنده ) أي عند الجزء الذي لا يوجد بإزائه شيء من ) تنقطع الناقصة ) بالضرورة فتكون الناقصة (متناهية)، لانقطاعها . ( والزائدة لا تزيد عليها إلا بمتناه كما صورناه ( والزائد على المتناهي بمتناه متناه) بلا شبهة. ( فيلزم انقطاعهما وتناهيهما في الجهة التي فرضناهما غير متناهيتين وغير منقطعتين فيها، هذا خلف. وهذا الدليل هو المسمى ببرهان التطبيق، وهو ( العمدة ) في إبطال التسلسل لجريانه في الأمور المتعاقبة في الوجود، كالحركات الفلكية، وفي الأمور المجتمعة، سواء كان بينها ترتب طبيعي، كالعلل والمعلولات، أو وضعي كالأبعاد أو لا يكون هناك ترتب أصلاً، كالنفوس الناطقة المفارقة.
The second aspect of the ways of refuting infinite regress: (We suppose from a certain effect by way of ascent) ad infinitum a series, and from what is before it, finite, ad infinitum another series – this is when the regress is on the side of causes. And if it is on the side of effects, we suppose from a specific cause by way of descent ad infinitum a series, and from what is after it, finite, ad infinitum another series. Then there result two infinite series, one of them exceeding the other by a finite number. (Then we correlate the two series), i.e., one of them with the other, (from that starting point, i.e., from that side which each of them has a starting point). So (the first) of one series (with the first) i.e., opposite the first of the other, and the second with the second, and so on. If (opposite each one of the exceeding series there is one of the deficient series) in the number of units, then the deficient series (is like the exceeding series), i.e., equal to it in the number of units, (and this is a contradiction). Otherwise, i.e., if opposite each one of the exceeding series there is not one of the deficient series, (then there is found in the exceeding series a part opposite which there is nothing in the deficient series. At that point) i.e., at that part which has nothing opposite it from (the deficient series cuts off) necessarily, so the deficient series is (finite) because of its cutting off. (And the exceeding series does not exceed it except by a finite amount as we have depicted it. (And that which exceeds the finite by a finite amount is finite) without doubt. (So it follows that both cut off and are finite in the direction in which we supposed them infinite and not cutting off – this is a contradiction). And this proof is called the Burhan al-Tatbiq (Proof of Correlation), and it is (the mainstay) in refuting infinite regress because it applies to things that are successive in existence, like celestial motions, and to things that are simultaneous, whether there is between them a natural order, like causes and effects, or a positional order like dimensions, or there is no order at all, like separate rational souls.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage introduces the second proof (al-wajh al-thani) against infinite regress, known as Burhan al-Tatbiq (Proof of Correlation). The method is as follows: For an ascending chain of causes, suppose from a given effect by going upwards ad infinitum we have an infinite series. Then consider another series consisting of everything before that effect (which is finite) but extending to infinity in the opposite direction. This yields two infinite series, one of which exceeds the other by a finite number. Then correlate the two series starting from a common endpoint: match the first of one with the first of the other, second with second, and so on. Two cases arise: either every element of the exceeding series has a counterpart in the deficient series, which would make the deficient series equal in number, contradicting the excess; or there is an element in the exceeding series with no counterpart, at which point the deficient series must cut off and become finite, making the excess finite as well, contradicting the assumption that both are infinite. Thus the original series cannot be infinite. This proof is called the Burhan al-Tatbiq and is considered the chief argument against infinite regress because it applies to both successive entities (like motions) and simultaneous entities (like dimensions or souls), regardless of whether they have a natural order, positional order, or no order at all.

Key Terms
برهان التطبيق
التسلسل
القلة والكثرة
اللامتناهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Burhan al-Tatbiq only works for series with a natural order, like causes and effects.
Correction: The proof applies to both successive and simultaneous things, with or without order, as the text explicitly mentions celestial motions, dimensions, and separate souls.

Checkpoint
What is the key feature of Burhan al-Tatbiq that makes it comprehensive?
A) It only works for causes and effects.
B) It applies to both successive and simultaneous things, ordered or unordered.
C) It requires the series to be physically real.
D) It depends on the impossibility of self-causation.

Key Takeaway
Burhan al-Tatbiq refutes infinite regress by correlating two series and showing that either they become equal or one becomes finite, both contradicting the assumption of infinitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just followed a logical proof that infinite regress of causes is impossible. Does your daily life reflect a reliance on a First Cause, or have you been living as if things 'just go back forever'? What would change if you truly internalized that your existence depends on a starting point outside this chain?
?
The proof uses a correlation between two series to expose a contradiction. Consider your own beliefs: are there any assumptions you hold that, if systematically examined, would lead to a similar contradiction? Are you willing to subject your most comfortable ideas to such a test?
?
If an infinite regress is impossible, then the chain of causes that led to your reading this sentence must have a first cause. Does that First Cause have a claim on your life? What would it mean for you to acknowledge that the ultimate starting point is not a thing but the Creator? How would your priorities shift?

8 min
Burhan al-Tatbiq Applies to Descending Effects Too
Rebuttal of an objection to applying Burhan al-Tatbiq to descending effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Burhan al-Tatbiq can be applied to an infinite descending chain of effects, and why the objection that it only works for causes fails.

Core Idea
Burhan al-Tatbiq cuts through descending chains just as it cuts ascending ones.

Some argued that Burhan al-Tatbiq only disproves an infinite regress of causes, not effects. This passage shows the proof works both ways: if effects descend infinitely, their totality must have an external cause, terminating the chain. Let's see how the objection is countered and why it rests on a misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection's premise
The objector claims the proof fails for descending effects because the cause of the whole could be internal (like the Necessary Being being part of the series). Read the passage to see how the author sets up the scenario.
The objection is summarized in the last part of the text.
2
Follow the rebuttal's logic
The author shows that each member is both cause and effect, and the totality must have an effect: either itself (impossible) or an external cause. Trace the two options and their consequences.
3
Identify the error in the objection
The objection mistakenly applies the proof to the side of cause, not effect. The rebuttal clarifies that the discussion is about effects, so the internal cause scenario is irrelevant.
This is the key dialectical move.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
Understand that Burhan al-Tatbiq is a universal tool against infinite regress, whether causes or effects. This strengthens the argument for a single, external Necessary Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( لا متنازلة في المعلولات إلخ فيه بحث لأنه إذا فرض المبدأ علة معينة صدر عنها معلول، ومن ذلك معلول ،آخر وهلم جرا إلى غير النهاية، يكون كل واحد من المبدأ علة من وجه معلولاً من وجه . فنقول : كما أن لكل واحد من تلك الآحاد معلول، كذلك يكون لمجموعها أيضاً معلول، لأنه ليس عبارة إلا عن الآحاد التي كل واحد منها علة، فمعلوله إما نفسه، أو جزؤه، فيلزم تأخر الشيء عن نفسه بمرتبة أو بمراتب وإما خارج عنه والخارج عن السلسلة التي فرضت متنازلة إلى غير النهاية يكون علة لا معلول له، فينقطع السلسلة. فخلاصة البرهان جار في المعلولات الغير المتناهية أيضاً، وما قيل في وجه عدم الجريان من أنه لو تسلسلت المعلولات من الواجب إلى غير النهاية، فحينئذ يمكن اختيار كون علة الجملة داخلة ولا نسلم أن علة الجملة لا بد أن تكون علة لكل واحد من أجزائها فيما إذا كان بعض أجزاء الجملة غير مفتقر إلى علة أصلاً، أي الواجب كما عرفت . فلا يلزم علية الشيء لنفسه كما في التسلسل في جانب العلة فوهم محض؛ لأنه إجراء للبرهان في جانب العلة، والكلام في إجرائه في جانب المعلول
His statement: '(Not descending in effects, etc.)' there is discussion in it, because if the starting point is assumed to be a specific cause from which an effect emanates, and from that effect another effect, and so on ad infinitum, then each one from the starting point is a cause in one respect and an effect in another. So we say: Just as each one of those individuals has an effect, so too the totality of them has an effect, because it is nothing but the individuals each of which is a cause. So its effect is either itself, or a part of it, then there follows the lagging of a thing behind itself by one rank or by ranks; or it is external to it, and what is external to the series which is assumed to be descending ad infinitum would be a cause with no effect, so the series is cut off. So the essence of the proof is current in the infinite effects as well. And what is said regarding the reason for its non-applicability – that if the effects were to regress from the Necessary to infinity, then it is possible to choose that the cause of the whole is internal, and we do not concede that the cause of the whole must be a cause of every one of its parts when some parts of the whole are not in need of a cause at all, i.e., the Necessary, as you have known – so the causality of a thing for itself does not follow as in the regress on the side of cause. But this is pure illusion, because it is an application of the proof on the side of cause, whereas the discussion is about its application on the side of effect.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection to applying Burhan al-Tatbiq to descending chains of effects. The objector argued that the proof only works for ascending causes, not descending effects. The author rebuts: if we assume a specific cause and then a chain of effects descending ad infinitum, each member is both cause and effect. The totality of these individuals is also a cause, so its effect must be either itself (or part of it) – which would entail a thing being posterior to itself – or external to the series. If external, that external cause has no further effect, so the series terminates. Hence the proof holds for infinite effects too. The objection that the cause of the whole could be internal (like the Necessary Being being part of the series) is dismissed as a misunderstanding: that would be applying the proof to the side of cause, not effect. The rebuttal reaffirms that Burhan al-Tatbiq runs in both directions.

Key Terms
المعلولات المتنازلة
برهان التطبيق
الواجب
المجموع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Burhan al-Tatbiq only disproves infinite regress of causes, not effects.
Correction: The same logic applies to descending effects: their totality must have an external effect, terminating the series.

Checkpoint
According to the rebuttal, what happens if the cause of the descending chain is external to it?
A) The chain becomes infinite.
B) The external cause has no effect, so the chain terminates.
C) The chain is self-causing.
D) The external cause must be the first effect.

Key Takeaway
Burhan al-Tatbiq applies equally to descending chains of effects, disproving infinite regress by requiring an external cause for the totality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if your existence and every effect in the universe depend on a single Necessary Being, or do you sometimes act as if things could be self-sufficient? When does your daily routine betray a forgetfulness of this logical truth?
?
The argument shows that an infinite chain of effects is impossible – there must be an ultimate cause. Has this certainty ever moved you to gratitude or awe? Or do you take it for granted? What would change in your heart if you really felt the weight of 'no infinite regress'?
?
You have understood that the proof cuts both ascending and descending chains. Can you identify a 'descending chain' in your own life – a series of dependencies that leads back to God? Have you ever tried to cut that chain by claiming self-sufficiency? Repent of that today.
